<div id="review_24322942" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/24322942" />
    <a title="Donellacandra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/471498-donellacandra"><img alt="Donellacandra" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/24322942?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Donellacandra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Donellacandra" href="/user/show/471498-donellacandra">Donellacandra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer24322942" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13869620449472277228">I think Laurell said it best on her MySpace when someone asked her what the book was about: <br/><br/>"BLOOD NOIR is about friendship and love, and telling the difference even when the boundaries are pretty blurred by conventional standards..."<br/><br/>"BLOOD NOIR taught me, and Anita, that we didn't know all that much. That, though Jason seemed like an open book, in fact, he'd kept most of his past hidden, at least from Anita and me. Did Nathaniel know more? They are like best guy friends, so maybe Nathaniel knew</span>
  <span id="freeText13869620449472277228" style="display:none">I think Laurell said it best on her MySpace when someone asked her what the book was about: <br /><br />"BLOOD NOIR is about friendship and love, and telling the difference even when the boundaries are pretty blurred by conventional standards..."<br /><br />"BLOOD NOIR taught me, and Anita, that we didn't know all that much. That, though Jason seemed like an open book, in fact, he'd kept most of his past hidden, at least from Anita and me. Did Nathaniel know more? They are like best guy friends, so maybe Nathaniel knew more, but neither of the men shared it with Anita. Of course, she did the girl sin, she didn't ask. To be honest, it never occurred to me to have her ask about Jason's past. He was just always there, our friend, our confidant, and sometimes lover for Anita. By the time I finished writing BLOOD NOIR I knew more about Jason's past than I do about any one's but Anita, Richard, and Jean-Claude..."<br /><br />"So, what is the book about? It's about love, and friendship. It's about family and the damage they can do to you. It's about forgiveness. It's about how far you would go for one of your best friends, and what you'd do to keep them safe. Yeah, there's sex in the book, and it's damn good sex, thank you very much. But it's not what the book is about. There is violence in the book, and killing, and kidnapping, and torture. But that's not what the book is about either.<br /><br />People get hung up on the sex and violence in my books, but just like real sex and violence, it seldom is what defines your life. Violence can define your death, but seldom your life. What's the book about? It's about love, and honor, and the price the innocent pay for the stupidity of others. It's about Jason letting Anita into more of his world, and taking me along for the ride. It's about a character that has been my imaginary friend for twelve years, finally being ready to tell me his story."<br /><br />It is not as high action as some of her other books, but it is a very important one that teaches Anita about the importance of friendship (not that she didn't already know, but it showed her again.) I think it made it clearer to Anita what Jason meant to her and how far she was willing to go to keep the people she loved safe (kinda like with Chimera).</span>
  <a data-text-id="13869620449472277228" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_339099797" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/339099797" />
    <a title="Carrie (brightbeautifulthings)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9868179-carrie-brightbeautifulthings"><img alt="Carrie (brightbeautifulthings)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1491349112p2/9868179.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/339099797?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carrie (brightbeautifulthings)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carrie (brightbeautifulthings)" href="/user/show/9868179-carrie-brightbeautifulthings">Carrie (brightbeautifulthings)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9868179-carrie-brightbeautifulthings?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer339099797" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8010275870473010081">I can’t believe this is my sixteenth review for this series. I’m still in the middle part where I’ve forgotten almost everything, and not yet to the point where the books are recent enough that I still remember (although I’m getting closer!). What am I going to do with my life when this re-read is over? There are overall story-arc spoilers ahead. Trigger warnings: death, severe illness, cancer.<br/><br/>When Anita’s werewolf friend and lover, Jason, gets a call from home that his father is dying, she agre</span>
  <span id="freeText8010275870473010081" style="display:none">I can’t believe this is my sixteenth review for this series. I’m still in the middle part where I’ve forgotten almost everything, and not yet to the point where the books are recent enough that I still remember (although I’m getting closer!). What am I going to do with my life when this re-read is over? There are overall story-arc spoilers ahead. Trigger warnings: death, severe illness, cancer.<br /><br />When Anita’s werewolf friend and lover, Jason, gets a call from home that his father is dying, she agrees to go home with him as his girlfriend and emotional support. Things go south almost immediately when they arrive, as a major wedding is taking place in town, and Jason is a dead ringer for the groom. He was mistaken for his cousin all the time growing up, but this time, it may actually get him killed.<br /><br />Jason is one of my favorite characters in the series, but Blood Noir is not one of Hamilton’s best. It’s a lot like Micah in the sense that I like getting a closer look at a character’s backstory and it forces Anita to closely evaluate their relationship, but it’s somewhat lacking in plot. There’s a lot of hand-holding and soul-searching, which is great for character development, but after a while it’s less than compelling.<br /><br />The wedding and Jason’s doppelgangers make the story more interesting than simple family drama. There’s obviously something more going on with these people, and while Anita tries to stay out of it, trouble pretty much follows her everywhere. However, the plot takes a weird detour in the middle of the book. In terms of overall series story-arc, it’s a good development, but in terms of the novel itself, it really throws off the pace. There’s just no way to incorporate it neatly into the rest of the plot, so when the family/wedding business resurfaces again at the end, it still doesn’t quite come together well.<br /><br />We’re also privy to more of Richard’s temper tantrums (“Are we Richard tonight or are we Dick?”), and I’ve been tired of him for several books now. He’s a bully, and that relationship is full-on toxic. The good news is that Anita knows this, and hopefully she’s about done making excuses for him. I enjoyed seeing more of Jason, but like in Micah, I expected the character development to go deeper than it actually does for a book almost entirely devoted to it. It’s a fun read for fans of the series, but I can see why I forgot it almost completely.<br /><br />I review regularly at brightbeautifulthings.tumblr.com.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8010275870473010081" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText17172428319301954885" style="display:none">Plot? Plot? Anyone? Someone? Please.... a plot?<br /><br />I've given up on Anita after almost every book since Narcissus and this is no exception. I'm not sure if this is the one that will truly keep me away -- it's better than some of the others, really -- but dear god, I'd kill for a flipping plot.<br /><br />Seriously -- this is the author who could make me stay up late needing to know what happened next. And in this slim little installment, we take a trip into sit-com land: she's got Anita impersonating Jason's girlfriend to make his dad think he's not gay(!?), a case of Prince-and-Pauper mistaken identity, anonymous sex with random weretigers, another pregnancy scare, and, oh yes, Richard has a jealous spaz Anita.<br /><br />Oh, and Anita gets yet more amazing powers and we discover that anyone who has sex with Anita gets more amazing powers because Anita is the bestest bestest mostest amazingest sexual person ever ever and she's way more powerful than anyone in the history of humans. <br /><br />Sigh. <br /><br />I give up. Again. <br /><br />Probably. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer34184451" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10016323139714707240">There is a lot of grumbling about this book and about Laurell K. Hamilton in general it seems. I like her books. Do they have a lot of sex? Yeah. So what? It's the 16th book in the series - and the sex has been graphic in most of the books. Definetly the last half have been pretty steamy. I think a lot of people picked up this book and wanted to be outraged or wanted to be pissed off before they even read it. Add to that the story line being centered around Jason rather than Jean Claude or Richa</span>
  <span id="freeText10016323139714707240" style="display:none">There is a lot of grumbling about this book and about Laurell K. Hamilton in general it seems. I like her books. Do they have a lot of sex? Yeah. So what? It's the 16th book in the series - and the sex has been graphic in most of the books. Definetly the last half have been pretty steamy. I think a lot of people picked up this book and wanted to be outraged or wanted to be pissed off before they even read it. Add to that the story line being centered around Jason rather than Jean Claude or Richard and you have the perfect mix of angry fans. <br /><br />I liked the book. I liked that she explored a side character because life DOES involve side characters. (Ok - in real life we generally do not sleep with our side characters...but this is a book. A story. Not life.)<br /><br />Nope - I will not diss Laurell K. and I will not diss this book. I enjoyed it. </span>

<div id="review_110867449" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/110867449" />
    <a title="Jenn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3957464-jenn"><img alt="Jenn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360078699p2/3957464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenn" href="/user/show/3957464-jenn">Jenn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=adult-fiction">adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer110867449" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16946558228179070958"><b>2.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>I remember that this was the book that changed <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30228.Micah__Anita_Blake__Vampire_Hunter___13_' title='Micah (Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter, #13) by Laurell K. Hamilton' rel='nofollow noopener'>Micah</a> from a novella to an actual part of the series. Anyway, this book was a little bit of a let down following <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30225.The_Harlequin__Anita_Blake__Vampire_Hunter__15_' title='The Harlequin (Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter #15) by Laurell K. Hamilton' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Harlequin</a>. While I love me some Jason, it just felt stiff and unneeded for most of the book. Nothing really new was gained and it was just more of Anita whining about her love life.<br/><br/>So what did I like? Well, learning more about Jason's past for one. He's always the comic relief, and I love him for it, but it was nice to meet h</span>
  <span id="freeText16946558228179070958" style="display:none"><b>2.5 Stars</b><br /><br />I remember that this was the book that changed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30228.Micah__Anita_Blake__Vampire_Hunter___13_" title="Micah (Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter, #13) by Laurell K. Hamilton" rel="nofollow noopener">Micah</a> from a novella to an actual part of the series. Anyway, this book was a little bit of a let down following <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30225.The_Harlequin__Anita_Blake__Vampire_Hunter__15_" title="The Harlequin (Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter #15) by Laurell K. Hamilton" rel="nofollow noopener">The Harlequin</a>. While I love me some Jason, it just felt stiff and unneeded for most of the book. Nothing really new was gained and it was just more of Anita whining about her love life.<br /><br />So what did I like? Well, learning more about Jason's past for one. He's always the comic relief, and I love him for it, but it was nice to meet his family - even if most were douches. And while the question of his parentage seemed pretty obvious from the start, it was kind of hard to tell if Jason himself knew of his parents secrets. I'd like to think he's not that stupid, but LKH has a way of dumbing down her boys for some reason. <br /><br />Another thing I liked was seeing Jamil and Shang-Da again. I've missed them. This goes back to my issues with the cast of characters becoming so big that we don't get to see ones we've loved from the beginning anymore, so when they appeared, I grasped onto them and didn't want to let go.<br /><br />Also, guys, there was hardly any sex in it! I know!!! I mean there was the pointless one the book opened up with and then of course some more with Jason in the hotel room, but it wasn't page after page after page. We get it, she's a succubus, can there be more plot now?<br /><br />But there were things I didn't like as well. Mostly, Anita. She's still a walking contradiction and just a bitch to people around her. She has no clue what she wants so she pouts over everything and then gets mad when people call her on it. Grow the fuck up. I'm tired of her constantly putting everyone in jeopardy because she feels uncomfortable. It's been years now, deal with your freaking shit. <br /><br />And then there was the plot of the book itself. Or lack of. The entire story revolved around Jason going home to see his dad who was in the hospital and not expected to make it much longer. But when Jason arrives, there's apparently a huge wedding taking place that weekend, and guess what? Jason looks exactly like the groom! They even knew each other in high school and were mistaken for each other alot. So chaos ensues because people don't believe Jason is Jason. Like why? It was just dumb. And we never even got to meet this elusive person who looked like Jason. His story was settled off screen. Along with Jason's daddy issues. So, cool...?<br /><br />But the thing that I'm most tired about is LKH's treatment of Richard. We get it. You were burned by a boy in the past and now you want to eviscerate him on the page. Well, you've done that and then some. It's getting old and it's extremely frustrating. He redeems himself only to make himself worse off on the next page. I was disgusted with him here and I just think the character should HeeHee into the wind.<br /><br />It pains me to rate this book this low. But as I'm rereading it, I'm just finding more and more issues that my younger self just didn't care about. I don't really remember what happens after this book so I think I'm finally hitting the point where I stopped the series. So, this should be fun. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16946558228179070958" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_46223661" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/46223661" />
    <a title="Lucy " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45923-lucy"><img alt="Lucy " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1300985055p2/45923.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/46223661?book_show_action=true">Feb 13, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucy " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucy " href="/user/show/45923-lucy">Lucy </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45923-lucy?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45923-lucy?shelf=2009">2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45923-lucy?shelf=urbanfantasy">urbanfantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45923-lucy?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45923-lucy?shelf=supernatural">supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45923-lucy?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer46223661" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7718497921420023653">There is no question that the last few books in this series have lowered my expectations substantially. The last Anita book I really enjoyed was <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/190361.Obsidian_Butterfly__Anita_Blake__Vampire_Hunter_Book_9_' title='Obsidian Butterfly (Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter Book 9) by Laurell K. Hamilton' rel='nofollow noopener'>Obsidian Butterfly</a>, partially because it featured my bestest best character Edward, and partially because it was all about the less erotic aspects of Anita's life--her preternatural hunting abilities and her necromancy.<br/><br/>There is nothing wrong with steamy sex scenes in books, but the problem with Laurell K. Hamilton is that when she writes them, she gets </span>
  <span id="freeText7718497921420023653" style="display:none">There is no question that the last few books in this series have lowered my expectations substantially. The last Anita book I really enjoyed was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/190361.Obsidian_Butterfly__Anita_Blake__Vampire_Hunter_Book_9_" title="Obsidian Butterfly (Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter Book 9) by Laurell K. Hamilton" rel="nofollow noopener">Obsidian Butterfly</a>, partially because it featured my bestest best character Edward, and partially because it was all about the less erotic aspects of Anita's life--her preternatural hunting abilities and her necromancy.<br /><br />There is nothing wrong with steamy sex scenes in books, but the problem with Laurell K. Hamilton is that when she writes them, she gets distracted and seems to think that there is no need to write anything BUT them. Which is why I could not finish <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/121927.Danse_Macabre__Anita_Blake__Vampire_Hunter_Book_14_" title="Danse Macabre (Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter Book 14) by Laurell K. Hamilton" rel="nofollow noopener">Danse Macabre</a>--and I finish every book I read, no matter how crappy. I could not get through a book in which literally every time anyone does anything it culminates in sex. And I mean "anything" like, walk into a room. Sex. Shake hands. Sex. Have a conversation. Sex. When your main character is a walking porn star, there's not really any room for plot.<br /><br />But maybe LKH get tired of writing porn. Because in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30225.The_Harlequin__Anita_Blake_Vampire_Hunter_15_" title="The Harlequin (Anita Blake Vampire Hunter 15) by Laurell K. Hamilton" rel="nofollow noopener">The Harlequin</a>, she went a whole 150 pages until her characters even had sex. Chock full of plot! It's a little sad that my standards for LKH are this low now (not that they were ever extremely high) but that's what it is. I now judge her books on whether or not there is any actual plot/character development at all. Anyway, based on my new criterion, and the sludge of porn porn porn that LKH has ground me down with over the last five books, I was hugely impressed with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30225.The_Harlequin__Anita_Blake_Vampire_Hunter_15_" title="The Harlequin (Anita Blake Vampire Hunter 15) by Laurell K. Hamilton" rel="nofollow noopener">The Harlequin</a>.<br /><br />And based on the same criterion, I also enjoyed the hell out of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2149535.Blood_Noir__Anita_Blake__Vampire_Hunter__Book_16_" title="Blood Noir (Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter, Book 16) by Laurell K. Hamilton" rel="nofollow noopener">Blood Noir</a>.<br /><br />This was not a flawless book. It was not even a great book. But even though it starts with a big fat porn scene right off the bat, afterwards it devolves into something resembling actual plot, and that goes on for a while. And when there are more big fat porn scenes later on in the book, they are tastefully timed and acutally plot relevent.<br /><br />There is some interesting character development (or what passes for it in an LKH world.) It focuses on Jason, who is my favorite LKH-verse character after Edward. We learn why Richard has been so douchey for all these books (and then he proceeds to show us that even without outside influence, he's just a big old douchebag.) Anita is on vacation, so she is separated from most of her man harem, which is always nice (Though don't think she won't add to it during the course of this book. Anita picks up new men for her harem like some people pick up tacky souveniers.) And there is actually some use of the <i>ardeur</i> that's interesting and doesn't make me roll my eyes. And the moment where Anita explores her anger was such a shining LKH scene that it was like a throwback to the old days.<br /><br />All this is not to say that the book was not flawed. Anita is still a big old Mary Sue, with her magical sex powers and the way she's super and awesome and her powers are so amazing and everyone wants to get with her, and everyone wants her as their human servant. And there's still too much coincidence and plot-hopping and melodrama.<br /><br />But let's be honest, we don't read these books because they're high literature. We read them because they're fun. And this one, while not quite as fun as old-school Anita Blake, is pretty entertaining.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7718497921420023653" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12521511324392868173">Blood Noir is #16 in the Vampire Hunter series is another sexcapade release with her friends. One of Anita’s endearing qualities is her ability to care for her friends even outside of the bedroom. Jason, a werewolf and one of her best friends and sometimes lover, asks her to go with him to see his dying father to support him and act as his girlfriend. His dad had been abusive to him thinking he was gay, which is anything but the truth.<a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[<br/><br/>Upon arriving at his home town complications o</span></span>
  <span id="freeText12521511324392868173" style="display:none">Blood Noir is #16 in the Vampire Hunter series is another sexcapade release with her friends. One of Anita’s endearing qualities is her ability to care for her friends even outside of the bedroom. Jason, a werewolf and one of her best friends and sometimes lover, asks her to go with him to see his dying father to support him and act as his girlfriend. His dad had been abusive to him thinking he was gay, which is anything but the truth.<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br /><br />Upon arriving at his home town complications occur because Governor Summerland’s son, Keith, is to be married, and Jason looks like he could be the twin of the governor’s son. The Governor is planning to run for President, and the wedding is the focus of local and national media and press. Since they arrived in Jean-Claude’s private jet, the press descended upon Jason and Anita. Chaos and mayhem on steroids. <br />This resemblance issue fooled the towns people and press to generate a fascinating sub-plot all of its own. Anita was identified as Jean-Claude’s servant as well as vampire hunter and executioner in national press.<br /><br />A Mother of All Darkness, Marmee Noir, sensing an opportunity to be disruptive, severs Anita and Jean-Claude’s connection so that Jean-Claude is unable to sense what is happening. <br /><br />Jason and Anita make a visit to his dad who has weeks to live and this meeting ignites Anita’s rage factor in the father’s contempt for his son and the derisive comments to Anita. She really shined through to put dad in his place standing up for Jason as her friend. They left the meeting with a request from Jason’s dad to stay for several days. <b> Yeah Anita!!</b><br /><br />Marmee Noir subjugates Anita after stripping her of her charm to keep Marmee Noir away and forces Anita to send out a call to every unattached were- tiger in the nation. In a total state of confusion over two days, Anita awakes battered and bruised to find two were-tigers she had coupled with unknowingly. Again we get the pregnancy phobia scene which spawns another interesting side-plot. Jason is grievously injured to near death during this two day battle.<br /><br />Richard shows up to be his usual jerk. The loss of connection was communicated to him by Jean-Claude. Angry conversations with Anita pulled some of his steam out of him, but I still don’t like him.<br />The new characters in this book were fascinating and generate a lot of interesting intrigue. <br /><br />As Jason was in the hospital toward the end of the book, his dad appears in his room having heard of all of the turmoil and injury to show that he realizes how much Jason means to him.<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I liked this book a lot especially since it was full of interesting side stories that weren't all about sex. This is an adult book with plenty of erotica, but not an overwhelming amount.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9117927977585285192">Sixteenth in the Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter erotic urban fantasy series, <em>Blood Noir</em> takes place in the Blue Ridge Mountains in Asheville, North Carolina. <br/><br/><b>The Story</b><br/>Jason's dad is dying from cancer and Jason is hoping for a Hallmark moment with his dad. Anita has come along on this trip to convince his dad that Jason is not gay and as moral support for Jason. Naturally, nothing can ever be easy and it turns out that Jason's cousins, the Summerlands, have gathered to celebrate Keith Summerland's w</span>
  <span id="freeText9117927977585285192" style="display:none">Sixteenth in the Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter erotic urban fantasy series, <em>Blood Noir</em> takes place in the Blue Ridge Mountains in Asheville, North Carolina. <br /><br /><b>The Story</b><br />Jason's dad is dying from cancer and Jason is hoping for a Hallmark moment with his dad. Anita has come along on this trip to convince his dad that Jason is not gay and as moral support for Jason. Naturally, nothing can ever be easy and it turns out that Jason's cousins, the Summerlands, have gathered to celebrate Keith Summerland's wedding. A cousin whom Jason so resembles that all the reporters, security, and hotel staff believe Jason <em>is</em> Keith. A resemblance that makes it easy to sell to the bad guys. Almost makes the Mommie Dearest encounter seem tame…<br /><br /><b>The Characters</b><br />Anita gets a new animal-to-call and raises a major stink for the weretigers all thanks to Marmee Noir. Richard gets his own nasty wake-up call when he calls the <em>ardeur</em> for the first time while everyone gets a new appreciation for Anita's self-control when she eats the rage Richard has within him.<br /><br />As this takes place out of town, most of the AB characters don't appear.<br /><br /><b>My Take</b><br />Poor Anita. She just can't catch a break. She has gotten much better about accepting that what someone wants in bed is not bad, it just is. However, her metaphysical issues just keep piling it on.<br /><br /><b>The Cover</b><br />The cover and title are confusing. The background of a soft, metallic, antiqued silver is gorgeous but I don't understand the point with the fuzzy-appearing upright scissors poised as if ready to dance. <br /><br />As for the title, perhaps it refers to the betrayal by Governor Summerland's people???</span>

  <span id="freeText10497531931123190366" style="display:none">I've read every Anita Blake book but have never purchased one. This wasn't an exception. I've honestly been getting a little tired of the porn aspect of this series, and while Blood Noir is steeped in sex, I enjoyed this book better than most.<br /><br />Blood Noir essentially centers around Anita and Jason, the werewolf. Jason's estranged dad is dying of cancer and he wants to return home before he passes on. Apparently, Jason's dad thinks Jason is gay and Anita comes along to prove otherwise.<br /><br />Chaos ensues as Jason is mistaken for Keith Summerland, who is wanted by some nasty people. Sex ensues no matter what. And Marmee Noir, the oldest vampire who is catnapping, pays Anita a pretty intense visit at the wrong time.<br /><br />Like I said, better than the last few Anita Blake books. But she could stand to tone down the porn aspect just a little.<br /><br />OH! I forgot. Richard is a pussy. I cannot stand that character and the sooner he's killed off, the better.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17482228226214853199">would you believe that a secondary character who we all know and love gets 2 books?<br/><br/>26 books into a series, and richard still hasn't one, but both jason and micah have two..<br/><br/>ok, now if you ask me this book should be titled jason, instead of the the other one,<br/><br/>but the 2nd jason book is just relationship thing. so anyway i'm getting off track here<br/>as the whole purpose or function is supposed to be jason's visit home to see his dad<br/><br/>however the entire focus of the book becomes jason's resemblance to the </span>
  <span id="freeText17482228226214853199" style="display:none">would you believe that a secondary character who we all know and love gets 2 books?<br /><br />26 books into a series, and richard still hasn't one, but both jason and micah have two..<br /><br />ok, now if you ask me this book should be titled jason, instead of the the other one,<br /><br />but the 2nd jason book is just relationship thing. so anyway i'm getting off track here<br />as the whole purpose or function is supposed to be jason's visit home to see his dad<br /><br />however the entire focus of the book becomes jason's resemblance to the sommerland boys<br /><br />so thinking about it, i guess blood moon could have been a richard book? <br /><br />ok, back to blood noir<br /><br />blood noir is a total mistaken identify and other things. <br /><br />so you come home from work to find 2 of your inner circle of lovers gathered around the kitchen table sad over 2 items of bad news<br />perdy broke up with him and tell me you did not think a mermaid and a wolf belong together, i have heard of mix marriages but i am very very sure this would not have worked...........<br /><br />so in addition tot he news about perdy being a control freak, you also receive word about jasons dad<br />so we have emotional support bdsm sex with jason and nathaniel.<br /><br />there will be more bdsm as the series progresses<br /><br />then jump on a plane to go with jason to see his father maybe for the last time<br />oh and jason just happens to come from a very very small town where everyone happens to be distantly related.<br /><br />the real reason for jason's dad's issues comes at the end of the book<br /><br />i will point out that anita did ask permission sorta kinda from micah and j.c before leaving.<br /><br />page 72,72 absolutely love the confusion with the press and the fact that the press thinks that anita has left j.c. for jason.<br />meeting jason's family was interesting<br /><br />and again there is some angst over jason and anita's relationship<br /><br />but again jason is the one person who can have a conversation with anita and she doesn't pick a fight with him or anything. as mentioned in previous books<br /><br />jason also takes this rare opportunity to inform anita of the consequences of her actions in previous books and how this all makes j.c. look to other masters of the city<br /><br />and then of course the news reports and jason and anita and jc. and irving trying to figure out to solve this mess.<br /><br />then of course the bachelorette party....... such fun.......<br /><br />interesting that the only way the bride can be sure jason is jason is to see jason nude..<br /><br />oh and the strippers at the party are vampire and were tigers<br /><br />the introduction of crispin and the beings of the trouble with max in vegas<br /><br />and then chapters 43 richard, richard and richard<br /><br />and anita making jason her wolf to call<br /><br />the issues with crispin and becoming a queen of the tigers<br /><br />and marmee noir saving anita again after taking advantage of her.....<br /><br />i love the interaction between anita and edmond............<br /><br />and the possibility brought up by the revelation of jason's father to anita<br /></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TgNjrv3LJ2idmGiza9CnKRnvFWMVVZIibAeLuyvP7DFU78U6utv1czeTkIxwCmEJmq8MgTobBqWF16xFjuszjg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('y/0MwiFHZDu/XdmWLSgCALXq5u6d5L14/LLtOvjuScTREapWZle2IBVWIak28sQgNqr/DLKqKf8VYsrEXcqWew==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer1276898408511728116">Laurell K. Hamilton is one of the leading writers of paranormal fiction. A #1 New York Times bestselling author, Hamilton writes the popular Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter novels and the Meredith Gentry series. She is also the creator of a bestselling comic book series based on her Anita Blake novels and published by Marvel Comics. Hamilton is a full-time writer and lives in the suburbs of St. Louis </span>
  <span id="freeText1276898408511728116" style="display:none">Laurell K. Hamilton is one of the leading writers of paranormal fiction. A #1 New York Times bestselling author, Hamilton writes the popular Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter novels and the Meredith Gentry series. She is also the creator of a bestselling comic book series based on her Anita Blake novels and published by Marvel Comics. Hamilton is a full-time writer and lives in the suburbs of St. Louis with her family.</span>

This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
